et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one has no power, then cut it into pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if it is administered to those we have said about abscesses that come in the sea;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if there is bleeding, let it be restrained with water, and let other remedies be administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose child had been dead in her womb; then another was sewn upon it and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time she got an abscess on her breast, which swelled up so much that it broke open and began to discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the priest, and I thought long, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong吸引plaster, and out came a bone, and then after a few days some more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very merveilled, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I examined the wound and put my hand on her bones until the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and for a long time afterwards the woman remained like that, occasionally dislocating slightly from her place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not recorded this chapter until now because when the masters encounter something strange, they know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the dislocation back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, with which one is bound in books; and at two turns around two shoulders of the two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, let the horns be more subtle on the constrictor, and be made of boxwood or ebony;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the post be one digit wide, and the edges of the trees one digit apart, and in length a palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in between the two sides are two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly joined in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two settings are driven into the mouth of the wound to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of boxwood or ebony, according to the appearance of tongs;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and has two heads two settings, as you see, a palm long, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see the wound open to all the instrument, then let the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging and her legs open,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then press together the two incisions in the armpit, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between his thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the entire instrument, just as you did with the tongs equally, according to the amount that you see opening the mouth of the wound, until the patient does what he wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated and have many variations in appearance; and when the surgeon has prepared them, his work is all the faster and more efficient for it, and it is also more impressive to his patients because of their variety.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair about the instrument that you have not yet prepared, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with some incense, and hold her hands over her mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she vomits, all the better.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take a pot and put in it herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as tansy, fennel, aniseed, chamomile, and pennyroyal.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All of these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over the fire. Then put one end into the pot and the other end into the mouth of the woman.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it sit until the vapors enter the disease; then make it sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then remove the pus gently.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and is not cured, command the patient to wet their left hand in oil of asses milk or in almice, and then she should wash it in the natural way,
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and find the pus; and when she has found it, she should squeeze it and stretch it out little by little gently, so that the disease is not dislodged;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it must be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pulled; it will then come out and be dislocated.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the wound is narrow, we have discussed the treatment of sneezing, and the fumigation of herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not healed by all that we have said, then beware of pulling;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary to tie what is at the mouth of the wound to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse her with four-fold ointment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if she can, she will go out; but nevertheless, when she defecates, there comes a bad smell from the stomach and head, and it makes her ill.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, you should use appropriate smoke: some of the ancients have tried smoke from watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one smokes out the woman for retained flowers and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is made of glass, resembling a cane, with a narrow head in the nature of things, and wide shoulders above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and the smoke from the charcoal, and the moth until it is destroyed, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born without their foundation pierced; instead, they have a thin, delicate membrane.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Therefore, the midwife should pierce that membrane with her finger, not with a sharp instrument, and she should be careful not to tear it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply a poultice of warm wine and oil, then dress the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, then insert a peg of wooden splint and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go in the chamber pot.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stopping of bleeding comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; then it must be stopped suddenly: then it should be treated as we have said with the wooden splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in ano
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas which come from under the anus are nodular, and grow larger than those that come from near the anus, or in the space of two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is one fistula or multiple; and when this nodule is old, it opens, and usually emits a white or thin pus.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are piercing; and they are caused by what comes out through defecation or flatulence when the patient expels gas, and sometimes a bit jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and they reach the hip joint, and the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows a fistula that is constant at the anus, and does not discharge:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and you should press your index finger into the anus, and push a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no crookedness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has crookedness, then you should insert a thin tent of lead or a horsehair until you feel the tent or hair with your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge, nor wind, nor pus, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	Know that it does not pierce; then hurry to heal.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has reached the bladder or the urethra, and the urine escapes, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it pierces to the hip joint, then there will be a bleeding vein up to that spot.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the pain is consistent, then it will remain as it is, and medicine or poultices will not help.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and with these persian fistulas there is no cure but hard work, and folly of the fools who meddle in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In one that is not Persian and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and the patient lies on his back; and he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, as far as you know the tent goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the pain is felt around the anus, you must insert your finger there.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if it pierces through the skin, then you know it is pierced;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not heal on its own, one cannot cure it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One can still heal some, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the helper who does this, he must heat the thin cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and he inserts it all the way into the fistula as far as the anus; and do this two or three times, until you know that the charred flesh is burnt, which looks like an owl's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat it with moist bandages soaked in butter, until the burnt flesh comes off; then treat it with ointment that softens and heals.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healthy, that is good. If not, it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent is inserted and does not penetrate to the bottom which is at the foundation, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of charcoal or of styptic, and you see the fistula in that which follows the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you scrape at the beginning of the fistula, and then plug it with cotton before the tent, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the tip of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the tent will be removed, and then it will fall out; then remove the charcoal that has been formed into a small ball, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus comes out, and flows between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For fire cautery brings together two things: that is, the scorching of these joined parts and the stemming of blood and the drying of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then, treat the wet tents with butter or ground-up matter until the places ooze, and let the fire burn into the flesh.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then, treat the wound of swelling veins with hot, dry poultices.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the fundament, and is distant from the body, put your finger into it, and probe it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between the two is the tissue or the membrane, or it is about to burst, then there is no hope but through the administration of one of the three remedies:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, insert tent and cure it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not go too deep, so that you cover the tissue that holds the fundament, and let the evacuation come through there as it will.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then heal, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance you will be healed, or you will remove that covering and cleanse it after it has been cut away from the foundation, either by a tent or by some pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then mend that broken bone in the wound as best you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study how to restore the wound and to stop the fistula in the part above the foundation: so it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes they are made into fistulas according to this method: it is when you push the tent into the fistula and it is on the side of the foundation next to the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	Take a tent, pierced at its tip, in accordance with this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he inserts a twisted thread through it, and pushes the tent all along the thread into the fistula until it reaches its tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the margin within the foundation, then pull out the thread from that hole as you would put your finger into the foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	And draw the head with a thread, and bring together the two heads of the shoulder, and tighten them one against the other, and leave it for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it sometimes, as long as the threads cut through the flesh that is between two;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not drain, then have it drained in every way you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to cover the wound with a bandage so tightly, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spiny spatumile, whose fistula they open, is very sharp and pointed on one side;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and not on the other, so that one should not bandage it too tightly, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are of two types: they can be inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and sometimes they burst and bleed.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	There can be one or more of them, and they can be inside the anus or at its opening; but those that are outside have less moisture.and sont grans et pletives, et sunt en grant dolour.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and sometimes they burst and release a little water or blood, and their color is like that of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is that you should instruct the patient to go to the toilet and push until the hemorrhoids come out, and then they will heal;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you are in a hurry, hold it with tongs or between your fingernail and thumb, then pull it out at the root.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the nails cannot hold it because of moisture, they should take it with a napkin or piece of cotton or camel's hair;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder some hot powdered medicines on top of it as if they were a cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauteries, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the fundament cannot exit, then cleanse the patient with a sharp and rough enema to wash away what is in the fundament so that it may exit clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient strains, and the thread comes out of the fundament, then the treatment is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And you should grab them with your nail or tweezers and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed and fear the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If you need to perform sutures in this way: take a twisted thread and thread it through a needle, then pull the thread from the top, and push the needle through from the other side, and then bring both ends of the thread underneath the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is wide, tightly wind the thread, then tie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do likewise with all the others, and leave one to draw off the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place over the wound a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerate, and place it over the wound, and instruct the patient to keep still;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let him defecate, and when he has finished, cleanse the wound with ointment and other remedies until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of dryness of the anus or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels due to constipation from natural causes, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	You should cut the skin at the tip of a spatula or your nail, so that it does not get moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then treat it until it is dry and healed as it should be.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	If it cannot heal, then restart the treatment with greater force than before, until it heals well and is scoured.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Antors is a small appearance formed under the body, and goes very deep;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the antors cause trembling, and it feels like death, and it comes over the whole body, more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a cane of a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place the feather on the vein, until the purple circle covers the vein all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand along the feather until you feel all around the vein, and push it in deeply, and squeeze the vein from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you can, make a cane of brass or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin beneath and broad above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you can, cauterize the vein, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or of molten and hammered copper; and sometimes they are made from these small and large instruments, according to those who use them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema, whether small or large, is placed on top, or the belly is bound in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has a hernia where the belly is tied, as you see, and the anus is pierced inside; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly where one puts the medicine in a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes;
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and it has between each opening an inch of space, then tie in these holes a strong thread of twisted thread in ten or so turns around, and gather the belly like a goat;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it with a strong thread to the instrument in front, then cleanse; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	Let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with a catheter of oil, or egg white, or something similar, then plug it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the minister squeezes his two hands together, as far as he can, then pulls out the catheter and releases the patient's legs from the wall,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, he should press as hard as he can; and if he sleeps for a night, it is even better.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catheterize him for diarrhea, and the medicine rushes to come out, then he should be given more until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or an abscess, then the enema should be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	This is the form of the subtle enema that should be used when the skin is stretched tight:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of wound treatment in the section on surgery; now we will speak of treatments using hands and medicine, according to the situation.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and according to what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The objects that make wounds are stones that strike, and sword and knife cuts, or spear, staff, or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or according to the places in the body, such as a wound on the neck, head, foot, belly, liver, and similar organs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you how to cure each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because their memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, one should be careful if it is from a blow by stone or similar objects, and the skin is still intact but the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you fear an abscess is forming quickly: then have the patient bleed from the head itself if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and let the patient avoid excess wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, then his food should be reduced, and he should neither drink wine nor eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place a bandage on the wound, if a hot abscess has formed, wet cotton in rose oil only, or in wine with styptic properties.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh and bleeding, and not moved by air, the powder I will describe shortly.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound has been moved by the air, then place on it some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that from a sword, and the lips cannot be brought together with stitches, then bring them together with a ligature, as I will describe for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it can be reached, and holds only by a little, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find pus in the skin, and it is not near the bone, then cut out all of the pus, and pour it out, then cure it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which is bleeding profusely, and it cannot be staunched by medicine, then cut off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then straighten it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy; you should put this powder on so that it burns until the pain has subsided.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the recipe for the powder is: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, three parts quicklime, and mix it all together finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it heals well and joins together without any blood loss.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bandage it well, leaving it bound unless it swells; for the medication is not removed until it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one should only cauterize with chalk, when they don't have incense or dragon's blood, but as long as the cautery moves the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the cautery has moved the wound, mix in some of this powder with it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply to it some digestive ointments, or barley flour made from water and honey, until it becomes soft;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat other diseases until he is cured.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, I will extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about fractures of the head afterward.
de la plaie dou col	of a wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is single, there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or arteries are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is nothing else to do but let it heal, and not put anything restraining on it, because it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	But use warm medicines, such as washings in lukewarm water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked washings also in lukewarm water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other moist stones according to this method.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it and bind it, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and the flesh is torn and full of bowels, then pierce them higher up.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if an artery is cut, and bleeding ensues, then ligature it, and close it up, and cauterize it as needed;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the nerves, and the windpipe is protected, through which the food goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the nerve on the side of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then gently stretch it, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with cleansing ointments until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then you want it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are bone fragments, pull them out as much as you can, and those that you cannot reach, leave them until the wound can heal.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and then open and clean the wound;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder I described earlier.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether there are any wounds in the head of the patient: know therefore that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	And if it is not deep and the wound is fresh and bleeding profusely at first, then do not apply the powder or ligature it to stop the bleeding immediately.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and let the patient rest and recover.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I apply an attractive ointment and bind it .ii. times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient sleep on the wound for 3, or 4, or more days;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, nor tremor of the heart, nor twitching of the limbs;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the bones in good alignment, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it therefore with poultices and other remedies until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and there is still discharge, then you know that there is a fistula; treat it then as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, on the front or back, then treat it as described above;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is deep in the bone, and has broken off pieces, then probe the wound, and draw out the foreign bodies if they are loose;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, let the wound fester, to lighten the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds in other members, the judgement is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, pass out through an opening;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the healing is more difficult, and sometimes the smaller wound is worse than the larger one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one puts the intestines back in more easily when they are warm;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, they contract more with pins,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore it is better to cauterize the wound, and therefore one cauterizes the intestine in its place along with the others.2
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that hernia of the abdomen occurs according to .iiij. ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the .ij. common hernias occur in the abdominal wall,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitching of other wounds of the body, and two other proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and nevertheless they are more appropriate with abdominal surgery, and I will describe each one and clarify.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and no intestine protrudes,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and it is easy to fix, which can be done in one of two ways:The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or for the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	moisten a sponge or soft cloth with lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in water squinting and cypress and spike
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and rose intestines until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this wine is restraining, and it is better to vomit to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling leaving, then boil the intestines in water or alt and bad wine are cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for through this the entrance is constricted to a small space;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound with the instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is bloodletting rather than cutting,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	which one should not cut without great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it with:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut into the curve and out again, and take note of the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines jump out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you put it back according to its natural shape in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you can, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	you should have the patient lie on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	put the head and the foot higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	put the understanding in that the ruptured part be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so you must apply what I say to large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, use whatever tools you have available:
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have at hand .i. pair of forceps that can grip the wound all around its edge,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the edges;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common method of sewing.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	You will thread one or more needles, depending on the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave a distance of about a finger's width from the edge of the wound and insert a needle with a strong thread through it;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce both sides of the skin with both sides of the thread,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, as far as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and gather the two heads together with the four threads;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then draw it through with a double thread around the needle from one part,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then gather the two heads of the wound together smoothly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave .I. space, and I pierce with another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then pull the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this according to how many needles you need,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is closed;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the thin needles pierce all the flesh, and the very thick ones cannot enter well;
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore they should be medium-sized;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and one must not push the needles too deep into the flesh and through the skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	that they do not cut and open the wound before the scab forms;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	then they cut the heads of the needles so that they do not pierce the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and they put tents or bandages on the needle heads to keep them from moving,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it requires only one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it involves joining the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the wound with one strong thread using a needle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all these pieces together [in a circle],
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then remove the needle from where you started, in the same way that one sews clothes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and insert spacing between each stitch the thickness of a little finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch severs the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that a man had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which he had received from a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm-width in size,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines protruded well over two palms in length,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and was the wound in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought him the intestines after they had been outside for 24 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound healed within 15 days, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And those who saw him believed that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat it with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and thread through the upper part just to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the skin straight-on, then put in the needle where you see the vein or where it is easiest to thread.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and have it pierce through from another angle on the inside all the way to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the technique for this sewing is that you sew as a leatherworker sews a hide,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leaving one end of the vein uncovered on one side and then covering it up on the other, until the sewing is finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of sewing, which Galen describes properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is to bring together the two parts naturally and smoothly,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	applying one edge of the wound to the other, in such a way that:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	they pierce an needle or sharp object into the proximity of the wound, and only pierce that spot,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two chins of the syringe;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and pierce it from the outside just into the inside,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as two chins of the syringe;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and the other from the outside just into the inside, in two other chins of the syringe that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the mother of all sutures, and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen says these words, and some testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should sew the belly with .ii. needles, each with its own thread;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is in the stomach,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	the incision is worse than other places in the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound all in blood, before the fire has moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if it returns to the intestines, and the gut; then put on the powder charm.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if it burns the skin, put on some ointment that is available until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut off the thread and tie up the sutures, and the myrrh;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you do not have medicine, then apply old cotton, as soon as it begins to drip downward.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it .14. times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will cause infection in the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if you need to moisten a light wool in tempered oil, or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the angles, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or swelling in the bowels, and this happens frequently,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then administer enemas of warm red wine, especially if the swelling extends to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine which is called "young" cannot heal when it is raw,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is because of the thinness of the veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the thread is cut from the wound, it draws it back also as the intestine does, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and turned red or black, then you must tie the area that has turned black so that no blood flow comes from it,
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligature,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two shoulders hanging from the part under the wound until they are relieved of the extraction when the nails drop, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the road of boiling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are pierced, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	one can repair it in some ways,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw a man who was pierced in the belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and was the wound on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and became a fistula, and from it came evacuations and wind.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to apply poultices until it was healed and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it healing, I doubted that the patient had discomfort in his belly;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimentalists say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take a large needle, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the needle has opened the mouth, put it on top of both lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if they pull at their base,
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then the head, and it is held so that it cannot be loosened,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another splint in after in the same way, until the wound is completely bound up;
et cout la plaie.	and bandage the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If they are absorbed into the intestines and do no harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread which is very thin,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then bind to the head of this thread a fine, twisted linen thread;
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then thread the needle with the thread, and sew up the wound, and reset it in its place;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of sewing up a dislocated joint is not without risk, according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great internal veins, there is no healing without subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that any wound or abscess, when it opens up, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and especially when it is deep and narrow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the green-looking hard and white nodules, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also shaped like a bird's feather;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	sometimes it is clear and thin, sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small, sometimes large;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of this in the section on wounds, that any wound which is not healed and has no scabs,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it comes only from one of the eight causes;
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is, through the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within it, and on the lips, that does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much bile;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the body is emaciated, and the matter is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good for treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the nature of the region, digestion is late, health is delayed, and it swells by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you about the treatment of a fistula that is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	You should know that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the eye, or the intestine, or the bladder, or any of the sides,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine in the back, or to any joint in the hands or feet;The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it affects the principal organ, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are of this nature are of painful healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have described, and you are confident in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it, take a tent of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, so take it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	if the fistula is crooked, then seek a subtle needle of lead.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because lead bends with the crookedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot pierce it well with needles,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you cleanse it through one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for moisture flows from one orifice to another and purifies it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then make the wound bleed as much as you can so that you may know if there is bone or nerve involved, and examine it thoroughly;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you know the exact location, whether it is near a joint, nerve, artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the ways I have told you, and the cup according to what I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove for the rot and decay that is within them;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the dressing as long as it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is very deep in a straight line, you must cup it as deeply as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I apply wet bandages as a treatment for an abscess, and tie them to the top of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medication corrodes the excess matter that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply warming ointments to healthy flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this method, then he should be cauterized as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve causes you distress in your limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and darkness, then cut it until the corruption is completely removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with salves until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and return bow as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not gone to the spring:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	uncover and desire as much as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus without pain, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other way, then let it heal through natural healing;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can extract with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if one extracts it with a suitable instrument for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, he must pull them all out, not leaving any behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	cut and dry, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then put on the wound something causing suppuration,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it fester around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have the bones more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you merely treat the corruption until all the darkness is removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then heal the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great deal of corruption, and it reaches down to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then cut away and cover up everything down to the corruption, then heal it until it is closed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg;
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and aid from it in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had a pain in his leg from something that entered the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came to the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and he had no reason to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but they looked at their madness so much that the abscesses opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they poured out a lot of matter and became a fistula, and many openings came from which all the body fluids flowed;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many looked at it for more than two years, but there was no wise man in the art of medicine who could heal it;
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called to see it, and saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated;
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what runs through the openings of the body with great speed;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the bodies of young men became red and had a yellow colour.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I set up a tent at one of these openings, and then examined all the openings,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that they connected with each other throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I therefore hurried and struck one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	And found it rotten and pierced, and the rot extended to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to be rotten bone, and I believed that there was no other rot other than what I had taken out;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but it would not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then begin again, and expose the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I cut it off, and I took pains to seal up the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not until I had copied around a palm of the bone, and I left it for all its length,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicine; and it was healed and sealed firmly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there is no need to repeat the treatment except for the weakness of the patient who cannot endure it,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and out of fear that he might die.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For despite the bloodletting, he was fully healed,
