et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in the place of the bone a hard lump grew, and he was in good health with no harm or discomfort anywhere, nor any difficulty moving.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if any bone of the body is broken, then one must sew it up in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a thread and hold it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct someone to hold it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and take another thread of thicker linen than the first thread, and tie it onto the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and you are the head, so you treat the corruption underneath,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the skin above where you see it growing, so that the growth does not blister the skin;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a burning brand or a hot table under the bone to heat up and cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must burn as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and burn again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is broken, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	disclose the flesh all over; then insert a burning brand beneath it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then cut from one side of the corruption to the other, and let the cut be as long as the corruption itself, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut through the joint, and cut into the bone on the other side of the joint;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the dislocation is in the continuation of the two joints, then cover it with a bandage;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the dislocation is at the knuckle of the hand or the foot, then it is very serious,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but you should still inquire about the dislocation, how it appeared to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but be careful that the veins or nerves do not cause any harm to you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and you shall know that there are many types of saws and knives to cut these bones, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of the joints,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason one must prepare an instrument for each type of work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and you shall know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to your knowledge of this craft,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and witnesses of the ways of sickness;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	then prepare the instrument you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders may dislocate due to internal causes or external causes.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated this erosion with medicine, but it does not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you should cover the affected limb up to the site of the erosion,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes through death, or through the greater evil, from the defect in the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, appearing as if it were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then comes darkness, after which the corrosion of limbs spreads from limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and throughout the body; so hasten to cover it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is caused by the sting of venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions, vipers, and the like,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is on the head or neck, then cover it, and do not give him any space to come just up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, then grip at the joint, so that the burn does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches the arm, then grasp at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there are no remedies against this, other than the amount of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And so it is with burns: if it comes to the first joint, then grasp at the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on the foot, cut off the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, cut off at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to kill the patient with a lash;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of lashing the limb, whether above or below, is to tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and one minister stretches one of the lines downward, and another minister stretches the other line upward,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you unscrew the joint which is between the two lines to a width of one and a half fingers, so that the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then the cup or socket, and place on each side a linen bandage, so that the socket does not touch the healthy area,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and comes to the patient another injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, then cauterize the site aggressively.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then tie the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man in a dream:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	there happened to him a darkness which seemed like a burn from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion started at the bottom of his big toe, so that it affected all of the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered his foot and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	a long time after that, the corrosion returned on the toe of the hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed impactions after purification of the body, but could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	he requested that I cup his hand, and I did not want to, as I had no hope of drawing out the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubted that if I cut his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's strength was weak; and he despaired entirely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he healed his hand;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I do not know what else to say except that one should make more of these things if there is a need for them.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they rupture and discharge, and the place remains hollow, just like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin on top is as delicate as a loosened napkin,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it does not grow to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called "healthy",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called  "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends to the bone, then it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and cook it so that you cover the whole skin, and especially when it is thin, just like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not harm it in any way.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you are concerned that the skin will burn, and there is no complete destruction,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with fat, then treat it thusly:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the breasts are large, and the navel which is in it has a foul-smelling odor.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then cleanse with an Egyptian medication enema made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take honey, and oil, and quicklime, in equal amounts, and put to cook in a vessel over fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	And then take some of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And use it as an enema on the breast, and constrict the orifice;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	Then let the medicine remain in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing it out;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this as many times as necessary until the breast is deflated and the pain is relieved;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes they are cauterized with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you must grind vine wood ashes, and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it run off, and use it to cleanse the wound as much as you know how;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, or the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if he is enema with water and honey or a little powdered quicklime.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you can enema him with honey and milk, as the honey has the property of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and wine makes the gut move.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	And when you have done this and you are sure that the intestines are clean,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if one enemas with what makes them defecate.

car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bowel is blocked, do not allow flatulence to pass.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that arises underneath the fingernail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or through a stone, or perhaps they grow in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is infected and one takes no care, then a large abscess develops,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and ooze pus until they reach the root of the nail, and perhaps they even cut off the entire nail;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corruption reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the shoulder becomes swollen and the colour is purple.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have described in the section, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	you must cut away all the excess that has gathered under the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the flesh, and starts to poke through, and bleeds,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then you should put the thread under the nail that is poking the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and pull it upward gently and subtly,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put burning and corrosive medicine on the remainder of the flesh to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with poultices until healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and draw it out, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth infected, pull it out in one go as previously described,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat with poultices until healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and biting, and it feels great pain, then you must heal it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut across the nail of the thumb,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the knife does not go all the way to the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on it to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	You must adjust what is born in some men's hands by chance is all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes it has bones and sometimes not, and sometimes it has nails,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some are born at the base of the joint, where the knuckle is in some fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born with a hernia in his navel should not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who is born at the junction of the intestines, by chance moves;

Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; therefore, keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For one who is born in the anus, you must first cover the flesh around it, all the way to the bone:
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with a suitable incision, and then cure him until he is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joint dislocations that come together come from birth, or from the dislocation of a wound, or from burns, or similar things.

puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two tents or pieces of cloth soaked in rosemary oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you can place it between two pieces of fine linen until the wound is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If this occurs in one of his hands with the palm, then treat that fracture as it should be treated.
Des vils	Of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large, wrapped vessels filled with melancholy superfluities, which come into many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it happens more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purgative drink made from woad, and then give him the basil-based remedy.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with fire is according to two methods: one is to cut with a knife, and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open a vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision is done in this way: first, heat the leg with very hot water until the large vessels are made slender,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg from the sick person's thigh down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then squeeze and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat meat that causes black bile;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and restart the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, which helps the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The treatment of this illness is as follows: shave the leg of the patient if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath and raise his leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cover the vein from the top of the knee to the bottom of the ankle, or in the area below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the shin, and scorch the vein from each side, until it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems as a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then pull it down underneath, until it is raised from the skin, and then it can be easily removed at the edge;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then scrape the skin above the vein until it bleeds, and then let it bleed for two hours; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then raise it with your hand, as you did before, and let it bleed at another edge, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another branch, or several if you need them, then grab it and cut it at the bottom of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull it and grab it until you reach the second cut; then pull it out from cut to cut, until it comes out completely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot pull it and grab it, then thread an needle with a strong double thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it, and put it under a stick, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and make sure it does not pop, because if it pops, then one cannot milk or raise it, and this brings harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have milked it completely, then place wet wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the bone is bent and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you must split it crookedly, but do not pop it; and milk it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife used to cut the vein is curved, and it does not slice, but punctures the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is very curved, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
De la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is winding in the legs, in hot areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it grows elsewhere than on the legs, and this happens due to the warts that develop under the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	like snakes and worms that crawl between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a great inflammation in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the colour changes, and the vein starts to come out, just like a plant's root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is dislocated, you should wrap it with a piece of linen three and a half yards long, and tie it tightly.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the cloth hang loose to the leg, and whenever it slips off, wrap it around the head again, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a piece, and wrap the remaining part around it, but do not cover the root at all until it has fully dislocated.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess or swelling in that place, and great illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of which it must be treated a little at a time until the end, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	sometimes this vein is treated with five or ten fingers length,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once a man came to me from whom it had exited ten fingers length; and when you grasp it, it pushes out one rod or peg, and it pierces all the way through,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and it is emptied of the matter inside, and medicine is applied to the area for several days, then it is cured as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein is moist, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot, or the foot itself,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it bleeds profusely, and from which it rains; therefore treat it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that grow between skin and flesh:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land, because it often affects oxen:
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and there is a small worm that arises between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body, going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it travels from one member to another, until it reaches the skin where it goes, then it jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	It is caused by the putrefaction of some humors, like worms and snakes and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And it is feared for its wickedness, because when it goes through the body, and rises to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him being treated and milked, he cannot hold back until he farts.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So you must tie the area above and below with a strong string tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then cut on top and milk it hard, and if the pus is deep in the flesh and you do not bring it out,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize it with fire above, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it makes the eyes run, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then squeeze under it firmly, and then pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and one must use a purifying remedy for the body from dissolving medicines for the corrupt humours,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if the flesh of the wound becomes putrid.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that affects some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and can move from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise up as a worm at her shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything else, like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that spot and settled in her shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it ran throughout the body until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that she was turning around the body, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered a lot how she moved from limb to limb like this, because I had never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not want to, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought it was because a woman's body is dry and their veins are exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and due to this, the wind is forced out.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear in those who are delicate and have moist bodies with veiled veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels the pain, if it seems to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	examine above and below carefully, and then press gently until the flatulence forced out of its place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it yourself,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	let the patient take flatulence-inducing pills, such as foul-smelling pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and depending on where in the body they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their tips is that there are those which are large, small, barbed, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those which have .ij. angles, and those with tongues, and those with parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which affects a limb, it affects according to two ways; or it affects a principal limb,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it therefore affects one of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you about appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must be wary of extracting this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces and penetrates the bone, and the spinal fluid leaks out from above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is scotomata and redness and blanching of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and loss of consciousness, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes there is discharge from the nose or ears; and sometimes they lose their speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is moisture emerging from the wound, white like pus, and also flowing out like blood from a vein.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears, stop the treatment and remove the arrow if it is still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of a wound when it is on the heart are that it is near the left breast and feels as though it were pierced into something hard, not soft.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And sometimes a wound becomes quiet like the pulse, and there is black blood coming out of it, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without a doubt that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that never leaves the lung are: spitting up foam without pain, and a swollen throat, and the patient changes color, and breathes hard and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits in the skin of the foot, it is among the small bones; and it causes great pain and great swelling and breathlessness; and all the limbs from the shoulders are affected.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something indigestible will come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the gut and feces escape through the intestines, then there is no hope for a cure or for removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder and urine escapes and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that this wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and hip and thigh and legs, and similar members, are safe according to several dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you to do, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man that an arrow struck him on the forehead, near the eye:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I treated it by pulling it from the opposite side under the ear, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I extracted an arrow that had struck him in the fatty tissue of the eye below the eyelid:
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	The arrow was lodged there, and he could only touch the tip with his finger,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and had been shot through with an arrow from a Turkish bow, right through the ear; the jugular vein was cut, and no ill accident befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he received an arrow in the throat from a Christian, and the arrowhead came out of his ear;
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the arrowheads, and extracted it so gently that the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I extracted an arrow from a man's throat, which had pierced his belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then if he had not improved after .xxx days,
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and he had no ill effects.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow wound in his back, and the wound is closed upon it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural dispositions do not change,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	it does no harm to any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man who had an arrow hit him in the face and the wound was sewed up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he stayed like that without experiencing great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I treated an arrow wound in the eye of a prince of royal blood,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was somewhat bent to the right side; and the arrow was all drawn out
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to tend to the wound after it had been sewn up for four days. When I arrived, I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I wanted to test it thoroughly, and I didn't feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt numbness and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied a digestive and soothing poultice to the area because the wound was swollen;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrow's path.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the poultice more often, and the wound healed quickly, and the patient suffered for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow for one day within his body; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied medicine to the wound with a corrosive agent for several days until it was opened up
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrowhead which was lodged in the wound;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visible to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and transgress the terms for four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then open the wound that I stabbed with tweezers, and pluck it from one side and the other, but it cannot come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I did not cease to use subtle methods and tools, until one day I took it with well-made tweezers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to how its shape came to an end in this chapter, so that I treated and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I therefore restored it, and the wound was sewn up and healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I will tell you about the extraction of some arrows:
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you may apply your remedy to what I do not describe, for books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters consider well very little, and what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	the new work, and the nine instruments, and the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows grow in the limbs where they are lodged according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumped out there where it entered is an arrow penetrating their flesh, and it jumped out some time ago.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, then leave it until the flesh around it is rotted away, and let the opening heal.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is lodged in the bone, and cannot come out, then leave it for several days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out; and if it does not, then pierce around it with a very fine awl, until the flesh around is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes to one of the membranes of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents I have described occur in the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even with the skin after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow reaches the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not stuck in the bone but only pierces the skin, and does not reach the brain,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without ill effects, if the instrument is used skillfully.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deep and cannot be extracted, then treat around it as I have told you; then heal the area until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged deep within the body and cannot be seen, then feel around for it with your fingers;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it out with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs holding it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then cut away the flesh that is pierced in up to two parts that you can reach,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or fold the ears of the arrow, so that you can milk it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, but milk it more fiercely.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then leave it until around the area it entered is swollen, then milk it, for extraction is easier then.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes you feel contrary, then administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting the nerve and opening the vein, and use whatever means you can to pull out the arrow without danger,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, with force or gently; and treat the patient according to how they were when the arrow pierced them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the best help you can give them; and if you cannot, then treat them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from elsewhere, or where some substance leaks from them, or the skin is swollen in an obvious way that one can see or feel:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then on top, as far as the tongs can reach, and then pull it out; if not, jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then rotate your hand rapidly so that it goes into the bone and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then try pulling again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a splinter in the wound, remove it completely.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it is cut, and you see to administer a bandage, then administer .I instrument with a thread,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then tie tightly,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, to tie an instrument with a pointed end going in, to aid extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, then you should cut all around the flesh where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then heal the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow pierces the shoulder or the foot or the abdomen or the bladder or the ribcage, and it is near the surface, and you can reach it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein and nerve, and then extract the arrow, and then stitch the wound, if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and heal it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the tip that grabs the arrow is also like a bird's feather,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of tongs for prying and probing is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins in the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	There are 31 common veins from which one can bleed, from which there are 16 in the head,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say, 2 veins that are behind the ears, called the two "ear-veins";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples, apparent;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are on the inside of the eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two gullets which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the .ii. veins which are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and .ii. veins that are underneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is on the left side of the chest, and the lay people call it the "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the method is called "fasting", and it consists of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is located on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it  "vein of the belly", and it is above the stomach,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one used for bleeding, which clearly opens above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The pulse is located between the little finger and ring finger, and it beats twice.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	There are three pulses in the leg: one is located below the bend of the left elbow,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second is at the ankle on the right side; and the pulse called "nesse", which is located at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg, there are three pulses below them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healing of veins that are after the ears is helped by old cataracts and emigration.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the healer, as I told you, and it is that you heal the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then press the patient's neck with your fist,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places down from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	take hold of your finger, and where you feel the pulse underneath your finger, press in there.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take a lancelet and pierce it underneath the vein all the way to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein upstream.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and grip the skin and the vein well, twice through the same spot, and let the blood flow until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then press and release it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding from the two arteries located in the temples is treated with leeches, as previously mentioned.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and also for sore eyes and excessive tearing;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of bleeding are as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel around under your jaw, and then cut in;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then gently press on the vein above your thumb, and push the lance underneath,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and open the vein at the top, and pinch it, just as you did in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the bandage, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	then ligature it tightly, and leave it until it heals; we have already spoken of their cauterization and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the vein on the forehead is just as good for old diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is such that the patient should twist his neck until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called a "spoon", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the tip over the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then tie off the vein so that it is healthy and sometimes work with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too sharp; and the wound is oblique, for the bone is close by, and perhaps the flame will break when it is very thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the two eyelids, which help each other, and with regard to tinea, and redness, and orifice in the eye, and facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the nature of their healing is that the patient should twist his neck in a certain direction, as mentioned above;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then heal it, and let the healing be through the transverse vein, slightly from the long flame, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the veins are subtle, perhaps they will break; then draw blood, as much as you need, and then ligature it with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding of the vein of the nose is useful for headache, and for vertigo, and for facial diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient tilts their neck, then squeezes their nose with their left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and takes a long, thin flame and places it in the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well, and now the blood will begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it off for a night, as it will heal quickly.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The juice of the stinging nettle helps with the tightening of the anus, and with hemorrhoids, and with varicose veins, and with many illnesses, and with skin conditions, and with ulcers, and with eye diseases;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of healing is such that the patient stretches his neck downward on both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and the master stands above the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a stool,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the vein of the long one quite widely, then draw blood tempered, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same on the other side, then loosen the ligature, and squeeze the veins gently,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the lips:
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of veins in the lips above helps with sores in the mouth, and腐敗of gums, and splitting of lips, and pain in the teeth and gums.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of this bleeding is to have the patient sit before you, and press his neck as I have said:
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at .ij. veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can identify them because they are black, and because around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	so cut both, and if you do not know them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	cut the thickest one on each side, and do the same to the .ij. veins above and below, for it is the same procedure.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bleeding underneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Bleeding the veins underneath the tongue helps after bleeding the head, and it aids in tightening the throat, and in diseases of the uvula, and in diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the bleeder are that the patient holds his hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on both sides for a black vein;
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed both, but do not go too deep, for there are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	Veins of the neck, which are usually healed, are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking with a very fine needle, or with a sharp olive-wood point, as thin as the eye of a needle, called "anasyl."
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and fine according to the size and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the olive wood point is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins of the head, which are smooth and contain thick blood and turbulence;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and that is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and subtle, used for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The sainier of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, aids maladies that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the surgeon must cauterize bleeding profusely and cauterize the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it pierces the artery, and blood flows, then it must be stopped as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not be squeezed, but trimmed like a horse's tail.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil does not open clearly, then you must stretch it and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want to cut a vein from it, or you heal the vein within the arm: it is made clear;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cautery with flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to find the place for bleeding, you should also stretch out the arm and touch the spot until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot on the inside, and then tie up the arm, and cauterize the vein with the flame;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and make sure you do not pierce the artery when you see the spot sunken in, for that is the artery; therefore avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulge out like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood;
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry, therefore, and place your finger over it firmly, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, for this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let him lie with his arm extended, and leave it thus, and do not move it until he is healed. And let him be in fear, and not move it until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not staunched and it flows, and medicine is not present, then seize the artery and open it, for that is where the blood retreats; and staunch the flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of bark from a beech tree, and split it, and take one half and bind it well in place until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding is staunched, that is good; if not, then treat it with a poultice, as we have said, of powders which stanch blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stanching is not effective in many cases due to the small wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	Let the bleeding of a vein continue until it draws blood from the head above and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the bleeder must be careful not to pierce too deeply and to find the nerve that is underneath,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and if it inflames and the patient becomes weak, and perhaps cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any men due to its subtlety, then you must heal it with the instrument anaesthetic; and shield the nerve to your best ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they cut it deeply.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	Healing of the cephalic nerve helps, drawing blood from the head, and helping the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and one must heal it with an olive or myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest location, and not worry if it is not right the first time, and one can begin again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, the site may swell in some men, when one fails the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done just to maintain health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the incision should be made in one of the three veins: those are, the cephalic, the fast, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should incision at the beginning of the rising of the stars, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of digestion are apparent;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should incision on the first or third day, after two or three hours in the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing that is administered to illnesses has no set time, but whenever the need arises, day or night, at all times and in all seasons.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a child beyond the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be bled in any manner, they should first cleanse the bowels with a mild clyster,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw off from the intestines the harmful excess fluids damaging the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor is there any cure for those who are too full of meats and wines, as long as they remain so, nor for the gouty or dropsical;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one desires to be bled after colic, vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequent intercourse with women, and exertion, staying up late, and fasting, or due to something in the weapon or from the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly draw off the humors if they are thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have that skill;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter the bath if nothing can hurt it to draw out the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein of the foot around the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard against work, pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and joyful, and let the healer be higher than those being healed, and rub the arm two or three times,
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then loosen the bandage above, for when it is too tight or too loose, he cannot walk.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area by hand, until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then wet the flannel with a little old oil, then place his index finger of his left hand on that vein under the armpit where he wants to bleed,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burst when cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which flow like cords into the body, and also such as are filled with blood.
